#  [](/thread/57749-trend-hugger-system)Trend Hugger System 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/57749-trend-hugger-system "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Edited Nov 28, 2007 12:26pm  Nov 27, 2007 1:14am | Edited Nov 28, 2007 12:26pm 

  * [ tkimble](tkimble)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2006 | [488 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=25926)

This is by far my most profitable system and very simple.  
  
1\. Works with all types of time frames (hourly, 4 hour, daily, weekly, monthly).  
  
2\. Create a MACD or OsMA chart using the following parameters:  
  
Fast EMA 40  
Slow EMA 50  
Signal SMA 100  
  
3\. The MACD and/or OsMA value will change for every price bar.  
  
4\. Use 50 PIP stop on all trades...   
  
Buy Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMa signal is greater than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
  
Sell Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMA signal is less than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
  
That is it. This system will allow execution of buys at the very low point of a trend and the exeuction of sells at the very high point of trends...  
  
Your only preference should be the timelines. If you have time to monitor the market daily, use the hourly chart. If not, use the 4 hour or daily chart. The greater the timeline, the fewer the trades.  
  
I have been successfully trading this system using a one hour chart.   
  
Enjoy,  
  
TK

In that case, every signal in your chart could have been profitable.

  * [#36](/thread/post/1731331#post1731331 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 27, 2007 7:46am  Nov 27, 2007 7:46am 

  * [ RickW00716](rickw00716)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [338 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=15358)

> [Quoting tkimble](/thread/post/1730724#post1730724 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> This is by far my most profitable system and very simple.  
>    
>  1\. Works with all types of time frames (hourly, 4 hour, daily, weekly, monthly).  
>    
>  2\. Create a MACD or OsMA chart using the following parameters:  
>    
>  Fast EMA 40  
>  Slow EMA 50  
>  Signal SMA 100  
>    
>  3\. The MACD and/or OsMA value will change for every price bar.  
>    
>  4\. Use 50 PIP stop on all trades...   
>    
>  Buy Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMa signal is greater than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
>    
>  Sell Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMA signal is less than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
>    
>  That is is. This system will allow execution of buys at the very low point of a trend and the exeuction of sells at the very high point of trends...  
>    
>  Your only preference should be the timelines. If you have time to monitor the market daily, use the hourly chart. If not, use the 4 hour or daily chart. The greater the timeline, the fewer the trades.  
>    
>  I have been successfully trading this system using a one hour chart.   
>    
>  Enjoy,  
>    
>  TK
> 
> Ignored

Thank you for this system!  
Do you take every signal it generates?  
  
If you got a long signal then a short signal was generated before you exited or before your stop was hit would you take the short and exit your current long?  
  
Anyone who has more chart examples please post them...pictures work so well in describing entries/exits.  
  
Thank you

Great seeing u again TK. Have been looking forward to testing your new system like so many. I was out of town and just got back to my charts.   
  
On the GBY 1 hr chart, (trading w IBFX) i had a high 225.43 and 225.35 at the close. Was going to ask if you wait for the signal bar to be taken out or do you enter the posiiton immediatelyh at the close.   
  
I took a quick look, and it looks that if you put a stop to take out the signal bar you will eliminate a large number of "color changes" and even further minimze false signals.   
  
Will take time to back test it. I trade the 4 hre GBY and EUR charts so those are where i will focus. Will look at 1 hr as well.

Looking forward to testing this system, tk. Just a bit of clarification though.  

> [Quoting tkimble](/thread/post/1730724#post1730724 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Buy Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMa signal is greater than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
>    
>  Sell Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMA signal is less than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
>  TK
> 
> Ignored

You also mention selling the peaks and buying the troughs.  
Now putting these two ideas together:  
  
Does this when the trough/peak has passed and each price bar MACD or OsMA is greater/lesser you enter another trade for each bar until the opposing peak/trough is reached then you exit all trades? Therefore, you are averaging in on the trend?  
  
Or do you wait for the trough/peak then watch the current price bar MACD or OsMA for the requisite length of it, and only enter once? 

FrankieB

> Disliked
> 
> This is by far my most profitable system and very simple.  
>    
>  1\. Works with all types of time frames (hourly, 4 hour, daily, weekly, monthly).  
>    
>  2\. Create a MACD or OsMA chart using the following parameters:  
>    
>  Fast EMA 40  
>  Slow EMA 50  
>  Signal SMA 100  
>    
>  3\. The MACD and/or OsMA value will change for every price bar.  
>    
>  4\. Use 50 PIP stop on all trades...   
>    
>  Buy Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMa signal is greater than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
>    
>  Sell Signal: When the current price bar MACD or OsMA signal is less than the previous price bar MACD or OsMA value  
>    
>  That is is. This system will allow execution of buys at the very low point of a trend and the exeuction of sells at the very high point of trends...  
>    
>  Your only preference should be the timelines. If you have time to monitor the market daily, use the hourly chart. If not, use the 4 hour or daily chart. The greater the timeline, the fewer the trades.  
>    
>  I have been successfully trading this system using a one hour chart.   
>    
>  Enjoy,  
>    
>  TK
>

  * [#70](/thread/post/1733069#post1733069 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 28, 2007 3:47am  Nov 28, 2007 3:47am 

  * [ billbss](billbss)

  * Joined Apr 2006 | Status: Trader | [4,301 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=9243)

> [Quoting purenirvana](/thread/post/1733050#post1733050 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi TK,  
>    
>  Nice simple system you have here!  
>    
>  I notice you prefer to use the OSMA rather than MACD for entries.   
>    
>  Can I just ask what does the signal setting on the OSMA indicator do? I know on MACD it gives the 100 average of the histogram bars and plots that on the same graph? On the OSMA indicator I don't see this however?  
>    
>  Also whilst we are on the 100 Signal SMA how do you use it on the MACD? Do you use it as an additional filter or not at all?  
>    
>  Thanks,  
>    
>  pn
> 
> Ignored

MACD = Fast MA - Slow MA  
In this case it is 40MA - 50MA.  
  
The signal line is a MA of the MACD.  
  
In this case it is a 100MA of the MACD.  
  
The standard MT4 MACD is an oddball. It plots the MACD as a histogram. In every other application I have seen, it is plotted as a line.  
In MT4 the MACD is a histogram and the signal line is shown as a thin line threading through it.  
  
Usually both the MACD and the signal line are shown as lines. They look like a couple of MAs moving together.  
  
The histogram, in most applications, is the difference between the MACD and the signal line.  
  
This histogram is what we are using here. This is what the OSMA is.  
  
Don't use the MT4 MACD. It is totally different than what you want for this system.  
  
Use the OSMA. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

When I see the accolades of others that have followed him in the past, I know he knows what he's talking about. I appreciate the creativity that people use to develope systems I find it very interesting and it makes trading more interesting than it really is (thats why I enjoy reading about other people's systems on the forum). But when I read something like this above it reminds me of when I was still trying to be profitable and I was system hopping all over the place. Its great when you find something that fits you as a trading method, but only time will tell you whether it really is for you or not. I just want to throw in a point that most of the systems on FF are about entry into the market. Caution is needed. You could trade off a coin flip which would give you 50/50 profitable trades and be profitable. My point is, entry is not as important as your money management and your exits. A system can have 90% probability of winning and you could still lose. A system could have 30% chance of winning and you could be profitable! Just knowing a good entry will not get you into the 5% team.

  * Nov 28, 2007 11:59pm  Nov 28, 2007 11:59pm 

  * [ paradoxical](paradoxical)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [1,186 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54706)

> [Quoting Porkpie](/thread/post/1734159#post1734159 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I appreciate the creativity that people use to develope systems I find it very interesting and it makes trading more interesting than it really is (thats why I enjoy reading about other people's systems on the forum). But when I read something like this above it reminds me of when I was still trying to be profitable and I was system hopping all over the place. Its great when you find something that fits you as a trading method, but only time will tell you whether it really is for you or not. I just want to throw in a point that most of the systems on FF are about entry into the market. Caution is needed. You could trade off a coin flip which would give you 50/50 profitable trades and be profitable. My point is, entry is not as important as your money management and your exits. A system can have 90% probability of winning and you could still lose. A system could have 30% chance of winning and you could be profitable! Just knowing a good entry will not get you into the 5% team.
> 
> Ignored

I appreciate the advice. Another person who trades forex for a living taught me that money management is even more important than the trading. Depending on your risk tolerance, I've learned that there's all kinds of money management systems, ranging from the conservative of not using more than 1% on any one trade to the risky of using variations of the Martingale systems. Or the "Profitsrup" system that I consider risky. For my own trading, I have chosen to use approximately 3% of my account balance on every trade. That way, I am risking less when losing, and more when winning. I always use stops, and with a definite 50 pip stop loss, I can easily figure how many lots to trade that would equal that 3% risk. For instance, 3 lots with a balance of $5,000., and 6 lots with a balance of $10,000. In other forex rooms, this topic was debated extensively and sometimes heatedly, with people sarcastically claiming that a person would never get anywhere unless they used the (you pick it) money management system. My choice was 3%, and combined with a good system. I am always open to suggestions and learning from others who have more experience and knowledge than I.

> Ignored

\----------------------------------------------  
My MM rules are somewhat similar to yours.  
  
Capital = $15000  
Leverage = 50:1  
Purchasing Power = 750,000 Units  
  
My Stop Loss on all trades are designed in a way that I only lose 1% of my equity should they hit.   
  
I would target 1 medium term and 2-3 short term trades for a day.   
  
Short term trades (SL = 5-10, TP = 5-20)   
Mid term trades (SL = 30-60, TP = 40-90)  
  
Currency Pairs = GBP/JPY & EUR/USD  
  
  
On an average day, my Win/Loss ratio would be 2:2. That's around 0.5-0.9% profit/ day.   
  
  
\----------------------------------------------  
  
Well, that is what I am working towards. Not quite there yet. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f911.png?v=15.1)

> 
> Your scenario is the kind that will make you money even if you win ony 50% of the time. I look for either a system that has a track record of about 60%, or one that wins more pips than it loses per trade. Seems that some are already dissing this system. Maybe they're right. But, from what I see, the wins on this one far outnumber the losses, and a 50 pip stop loss would have saved you during the "January" scenario. I have to think that tkimble knows what he's doing, since he's come up with other good systems. Seems like people look for the holy grail here, and look for faults in other peoples systems. No system is going to be 100%, or perfect for all times.
> 
> Ignored

I think tkimble would have had a 150 pip trailing stop in the January scenario and (I haven't looked back) made a few hundred extra pips. It seems to me that if we know about this phenomenon - it's as though the indicator has nowhere to go after the price continues to rise - it can be used to advantage. I hope you don't think I was "dissing". I don't want to change anything. I just wanted to point out something. 

Gone to a better place

Nearing short signal. There are times when the price bar MACD or OsMA values are identical but change as the following bar matures. That is the case as I am typing. I have taken the short GBP/JPY signal at 228.46.  
  
This equates to a 390 PIP gain...

  * Nov 29, 2007 12:31pm  Nov 29, 2007 12:31pm 

  * [ tkimble](tkimble)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Nov 2006 | [488 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=25926)

> [Quoting billbss](/thread/post/1736055#post1736055 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> The bar hasn't completed for the short.  
>  I thought you waited for the bar to close.
> 
> Ignored

That is correct unless both bars are of equal value, then I will take the trade.  
  
The two previous bars have a value of .3996 - I accept this as a signal becuase typically at the conclusion of the current bar, the previous bar's value will have dropped below .3996. This sometimes occurs due to a lagging OsMA or MACD calculation.  
  
TK...

> [Quoting Lincoln10](/thread/post/1736095#post1736095 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I'm no expert but it sounds like he's saying that if the current bar is down (but hasn't closed) and the previous two bars are of equal value (in this case 0.396 I think) then he will exit because normally the second bar of the two will readjust lower due to the lagging calculations of the OSMA and MACD.  
>    
>  TK am I in the ballpark with this answer?
> 
> Ignored

This is an excellent example of entry management. You now see that the last bar in fact confirmed the short signal. Had you waited till the end of the last bar, you would have went short at 228.18 instead of taking the short position when the previous bars were equal at a price of 228.48 and you would now have been stopped out since the market has passed the 228.68 mark which is where your stop would have been placed.  
  
While this trade is currently position unfriendly, at least we are not yet stopped out and still have a chance for a profitable trade...  
  
TK

It's a little too complicated to go into here.  
Basically after you get the signal to enter the trade (in this case tonight it was a lower OSMA bar), you use a 1MA and 5MA on the 1M or 5M chart to actually enter.  
Using that method tonight would have gotten you in at 228.64.

So essentially it is another method of going short since you enter your position before a short signal was given on this time frame?  
  
Honestly, after i refine a system, i have had a tendancy to figure out how to get into trades earlier, but ultimately i concluded that what i am really doing is adjusting the system and thus skewing results. It makes total sense to use different timeframes to get in earlier, i just haven't been able to do it consistently, plus i don't have as much confidence in the trade as i don't have a true signal from the system that i tested.   
  
Good trading,  
  
Jimno

  * Nov 29, 2007 3:03pm  Nov 29, 2007 3:03pm 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

billbss  
  
Sounds like it could be a good filter for the new "two equal bars" rule. Though I don't know if I would use a 1 MA and 5 MA on such a volatile pair as GBP/JPY. Maybe a 3 SMA and 8 SMA based on HLC/3 (pivot point moving averages) would be a little smoother. I'd also look at prior price action to see if price is finding support/resistance at the 3 SMA.   
  
If you notice the prior uptrend before the short signal, the price stayed right on top of the 3 SMA the whole move up. Thats what I like to see.  
  
Also it's nice if price stays away from the 8 SMA.

  * [#132](/thread/post/1736319#post1736319 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 29, 2007 3:43pm  Nov 29, 2007 3:43pm 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

Gotcha. I just finished reading his posts throughout the _entire_ thread. I like what he says. Essentially, when applied to this method we would wait for the OsMA signal (color change) then drop to the 1 or 5 minute chart and look for a 1 MA to cross the 5 MA (Linear Weighted, HL/2) in the direction of our signal. We would enter at the market and place our stop at the 5 MA. Once we were in profit an amount equal to our spread (7 pips), we would move our stop to breakeven. Thus minimizing our risk on any trade to a few pips (about 8 pips in tonights case).  
  
I like it. We would need to adjust our TP levels. If we had waited for a reverse cross of the 1 MA and 5 MA we would have taken a 7 pip profit (when our max profit was 42 pips). I should also note that if we didn't take a profit at the cross we would have been stopped out at 07:55 (if stop was placed at 228.50).  
  
May be a good way to scalp some pips on few trades while the longer term trade plays out.  
  
Also my prices may differ from yours, I'm using MT4 on Alpari. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#133](/thread/post/1736337#post1736337 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 3:53pm  Nov 29, 2007 3:49pm | Edited 3:53pm 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

Additionally, had we been stopped out from first trade and re-entered on next downward cross we would have been stopped out on the next bar and finally on the third downward cross at 228.18 we would have re-entered and would now be sitting on a 57+ pip profit. Not bad. Not to mention the previous 2 trades were stopped out at _**breakeven**_.  
  
Only downside to this is having to sit at the monitor watching for crosses.

  * [#135](/thread/post/1736420#post1736420 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 29, 2007 4:28pm  Nov 29, 2007 4:28pm 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

Hmm. On my chart I get the stochastics dropping from overbought levels at 6:30 GMT (after the close of the first down OsMA bar). At that time the moving averages crossed and the 5 MA was at 228.50. According to nanningbob we would place our stop there until we had a profit equal to our spread (7 pips) then we move our stop to breakeven (which we eventually would have in this case).  
  
Now, according to my chart, at around 7:55 GMT, price hit 228.50 which would have activated our stop. Right?  
  
Then I was thinking we could have re-entered after the next downward cross as the stochastics approached the 80 line and reversed. If we had placed our stop at the 5 MA again we would have been stopped.  
  
On the third downward cross (8:00 GMT), the stochastics didn't quite reach the 80 line but if you draw a trend line along the stochastic highs you could see a downward trend. I took this as a bearish indicator and took the third trade which proved profitable (and still is).  
  
Again my charts my differ from yours. Im using the GBP/JPY 1H for long term signal and 5M for entry. Im also using the MT4 Stochastic Oscillator.  
  
Whatever the case may be though, I appreciate the link to the thread.

  * Nov 29, 2007 4:39pm  Nov 29, 2007 4:39pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar4502_4.gif) james275](james275)

  * | Joined Nov 2005  | Status: Trader | [129 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=4502)

Bill/Lincoln ; I just put together a screen with all time frames on them and the simple OSMA indicator. When i look at all of them it gets very confusing unless you know how to properly trade different time frames. When to get in, when to get out... Some show long, some show short.  
  
Bill, if we simply used the 30 minute chart, this system would have gotten us in "early" compared to the 1 hr chart. my IBFX chart shows a short of 228.64 on the 30 minute chart. If you had traded the 15 minute chart, you would have shorted at 228.84 after one stop out. The 5 min is another entry. So IMO the real question is, "What time frame are you REALLY trading?" Seems to me u are trading the equivalent of the 30 min system and bringing in another system to enter.....Honestly very confusing why you would make such a simple system so complicated to trade.  
  
Personally, i am trading the 4 hr charts and am still long. Now for me to trade anything else if fine, but i better have back or forward tested it to understand how it works.   
  
I find that so many of us tend to take a simple system and want to make it so complicated. TK's system (S) are so simple, and work. Like all systems, you take your lumps, but they are profitable. They certainly can be refined and adjusted and TK encourages all traders to make it work for them.   
  
Just my 2 cents, but the simpliar and clearer rules the better, but nothing stops us from adjusting them together or for ourselves.   
  
Thanks..  
  
Jimno

  * [#139](/thread/post/1736460#post1736460 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 29, 2007 4:47pm  Nov 29, 2007 4:47pm 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

I definately agree. TK's system works fine as it is. The purpose of using nanningbob's strategy is to minimize the risk. (i.e. the 50 pip stop). According to nanningbob, he will enter a trade with a very small stop loss (10 pips) as long as his indicators line up. If he's wrong he is usually stopped out at breakeven (free trade). But when he's right he makes a decent profit with very limited risk.  
  
I think that should be the goal of every trader regardless of the system traded.  
  
In a nutshell, if you can make most of your wrong trades - _free trades_ \- then no matter what system you use you should come out on top.  
  
I also agree that we're gettin off topic, so I'll stop posting on this particular matter. Plus I'm going to bed.

  * [#140](/thread/post/1736471#post1736471 "Post Permalink")

  * Nov 29, 2007 4:52pm  Nov 29, 2007 4:52pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43707_8.gif) DXTrade](dxtrade)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Take Five | [755 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43707)

**Don't fix it if it ain't broken!**  
  
I was reading hundreds or thousands of posts in the last weeks of great trading systems and setups here and in other forums.  
So many peoples putting their brains here, trying to find a way to beat the difficult Forex market. Tough enemy.  
So there are so many systems - better or worse - with different ways to attack the market depending of the temperament of each trader. Some like it hot and aggressive hanging 16 hours in front of their screens, some trade on dailies with a quick look on the charts in the morning.  
  
But one thing I have been observing is the following:  
  
* There is someone posting a new thread about a system he is using personally and successfully.  
* Then the thread gets busy and a lot of qualified guys (thats not ironic!) try to help and make the whole thing better.  
* After 1,000 post you barely have the originator of the system posting anymore as he still has his original chart and setup from post #1 still trading successfully.  
* After reading post 1,500 the whole system has changed to something completely different and nobody remembers the basic idea anymore and more post from peoples coming in asking what the hell is the right and best setup for this as there are soooo many different in the thread!  
  
Please, this is not to criticize the work and effort of all the great guys here trying to improve the trading methods. My personal conclusion is nevertheless:  
Choose a system which fits your trading style and temperament, read the post #1 of the thread and apply it. You will be fine!  
  
This thread is a perfect example. Read post #1. The rest is just fixing something that ain't broken!  
  
Thanks TKimble ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)  
  
Good luck all... 

"The only successful substitute for brains is silence."

hi my indicator that i use is based on a similar thing to the way your using the histogram on the macd........take a look tell me what you think.  
  
I have traded a very similar system to this using my own indicator posted below. Some and most days it works like magic, but then there are days like the macd, and all oscillators for that matter, it lags and does not seem to follow the market well. But then i guess this is where your risk model comes into play.

  * Nov 30, 2007 12:01am  Nov 30, 2007 12:01am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar49624_4.gif) fiveshorts](fiveshorts)

  * | Joined Sep 2007  | Status: Where there's cash there's hope. | [84 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=49624)

> [Quoting DXTrade](/thread/post/1736471#post1736471 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> **Don't fix it if it ain't broken!**  
>    
>  * There is someone posting a new thread about a system he is using personally and successfully.  
>  * Then the thread gets busy and a lot of qualified guys (thats not ironic!) try to help and make the whole thing better.  
>  * After 1,000 post you barely have the originator of the system posting anymore as he still has his original chart and setup from post #1 still trading successfully.  
>  * After reading post 1,500 the whole system has changed to something completely different and nobody remembers the basic idea anymore and more post from peoples coming in asking what the hell is the right and best setup for this as there are soooo many different in the thread!
> 
> Ignored

Very well observed and very well put. I've been bothered by exactly the same thing. You rarely see the originators of these threads still actively involved in the threads they've started after 10 or 20 pages. It's very frustrating if you come into a thread a bit late and want to be able to ask some new questions, as the only people willing and able to answer are usually those who've somehow made the thread their own and are working off a vague facsimile of the original (usual simple) system.  
  
Now, I'm torn about this. On the one hand it's an expression of a free and evolving dynamic where seeds are planted and allowed to grow how they will. On the other hand it's symptomatic of a world where a lot of folks have way too much time on their hands (probably waiting for a four hour candle to close :-) and just spend that time messing with everything.  
  
Here's where it gets tricky for me, 'cos I'm a sucker for tinkering with everything _myself_ , so I can't be too judgemental. As soon as I'd built a "Trend Hugger" template, I was slapping pivots and fibs and bollingers and logical numbers and EMAs on it to try and "improve" it. What is _that_ about?? Why can't I just leave s*#t alone?  
  
After a while the tkimbles of this world leave us to get on with it.  
  
Like putting a Ming vase in the monkey cage...  
  
I'll shutup now.

  * Nov 30, 2007 5:24am  Nov 30, 2007 5:24am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar4502_4.gif) james275](james275)

  * | Joined Nov 2005  | Status: Trader | [129 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=4502)

> [Quoting bjk2801](/thread/post/1737671#post1737671 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> A entered into a short trade with the OsMA headed down & price down. The next couple of OsMA bars were down. Why did I get stopped out? I thought this was only possible if the bars' value increased and changed direction? Please help!! Thanks.
> 
> Ignored

BJ....Just because the OSMA bars go up or down doesn't mean you won't get stopped out. There are times that the bars go up and price stays flat or goes down. That is a divergence pattern on this indicator. Or OSMA goes down and price doesn't . Sometime this happens, and sometimes it can be extended. This system will have that issue, and therefore the initial stop (not the trailing one) is set at 50 pips. You do this to protect your capital and limit your risk. The good news is that when u enter your trade, more often it will take off in your direction and you can make 10 times that amount if you properly manage the trade, which means bringing the stop to Break even (BE ) after u reach 150 pips above your entry and then continue to manage it as price goes in your direction. Eventually, either your trailing stop will get hit, or you will receive an opposite signal, both of which should close your position.  
  
Maybe 4 out of 10 trades results in a 50 pip loss each. You will more than make up for that on the other 6.   
  
Look at how TK managed his last trade. He entered, trailed his stop and manged his trade. at one time he probably had almost a 300 pip profit, but he stuck to the system, and profited 125 pips. Now he is waiting for the next.   
  
Originally Posted by **tkimble** [](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=1737489#post1737489)<http://www.forexfactory.com/images/buttons/viewpost.gif>  
_I was stopped out at 227.21 (150 PIP Trailing Stop) for a 125 PIP profit. Waiting for long signal...  
  
_  
I would encourage u not to be worried about being stopped out. It is PART OF THE SYSTEM. Just trade it like it is outlined, and the results u will experience will make you happy....  
  
good trading...  
  
Jimno

Do you enter trades at the very top (high price - Short) and wait for the bottom of the valley (low price - long) or can you enter on the way up and down? The system as TK has outlined is based on his experience using a 1 hour timeframe. It works for him. Maybe this time frame doesn't work for you. I highlighted in **RED** something you said. A HUGE part of trading is the execution of the system u use. You need PATIENCE and Consistency to be successful in this business. Sounds like you may be wanting to jump in or out of the market too soon or late because u are having a hard time waiting for market to do its' thing after you put on a trade.   
  
Personally, i am still experimenting with different time frames. I normally trade on the 4hr/daily time frames, but this is another one of TK's addicting systems that gets me going. LOL. So i am looking at other time frames as well.   
  
But the golden standard in this thread is the 1 hr. I am back and forward testing this for myself, and it is really is TK's best system to date. Together, like in his other threads, the system may get tweeked because of great input and ideas from others on this thread.   
  
  
  
Goodtrading...  
  
jimno

gbpjpy (still the very best in terms of profitability)  
nzdjpy  
eurjpy  
usdcad  
audusd (better on the 30 min chart)

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar4502_4.gif) james275](james275)

> [Quoting bjk2801](/thread/post/1737909#post1737909 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Still puzzled...the next bar can be only slightly down. Do you wait for the close of the first bar (in the opposite direction) and verification of the second bar (opening in the same changed direction) for entry? My point is that when you look at OsMA in real time, each bar is only slightly different when it changes direction. Do you look for a greater value change? So you can only enter at the top of an hour, correct? So if you get stopped out, do you have to wait until the current trend reverses (this would probably be many hours, right? Thanks.
> 
> Ignored

  
I think Sky has it right. Look at his post just above and very nice screen shot that shows it. Let see if i can answer some other questions.   
  
1\. Enter at the close of the first bar showing an OSMA (not price) in the oppostie direction, there is no verification of the second bar. Or you could say enter right at the OPen of the bar following the change.  
  
2\. The amount of change of the OSMA bar may help you recoqnize when the signal bar may come, but wait for the close of the bar. TK also will consider it a signal when the OSMA bars are equal.   
  
3\. Yes, for the 1 hr system, you would enter at the top of an hour when a signal is received.  
  
4\. I don't think TK has answered what he does if he is stopped out, and how would get back in. TK? I know what i do, but i am still looking at 2 different ways.   
  
Hope this helps...  
  
Jimno

> [Quoting james275](/thread/post/1737831#post1737831 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> BJ....Just because the OSMA bars go up or down doesn't mean you won't get stopped out. There are times that the bars go up and price stays flat or goes down. That is a divergence pattern on this indicator. Or OSMA goes down and price doesn't . Sometime this happens, and sometimes it can be extended. This system will have that issue, and therefore the initial stop (not the trailing one) is set at 50 pips. You do this to protect your capital and limit your risk. The good news is that when u enter your trade, more often it will take off in your direction and you can make 10 times that amount if you properly manage the trade, which means bringing the stop to Break even (BE ) after u reach 150 pips above your entry and then continue to manage it as price goes in your direction. Eventually, either your trailing stop will get hit, or you will receive an opposite signal, both of which should close your position.  
>    
>  Maybe 4 out of 10 trades results in a 50 pip loss each. You will more than make up for that on the other 6.   
>    
>  Look at how TK managed his last trade. He entered, trailed his stop and manged his trade. at one time he probably had almost a 300 pip profit, but he stuck to the system, and profited 125 pips. Now he is waiting for the next.   
>    
>  Originally Posted by **tkimble** [](http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?p=1737489#post1737489)<http://www.forexfactory.com/images/buttons/viewpost.gif>  
>  _I was stopped out at 227.21 (150 PIP Trailing Stop) for a 125 PIP profit. Waiting for long signal..._  
>    
>    
>  I would encourage u not to be worried about being stopped out. It is PART OF THE SYSTEM. Just trade it like it is outlined, and the results u will experience will make you happy....  
>    
>  good trading...  
>    
>  Jimno
> 
> Ignored

You are correct...

  * [ TraderGeek](tradergeek)

Just started testing this system yesterday. I have made 2 rookie mistakes so far:  
  
1\. Last night before I went to bed at about 6:00 GMT, it really looked like it was going to turn and the bars were close to equal. So I went ahead and went long. I was right as it did finally turn at 11:00 GMT, but I got wicked out of my 50 pip stop in the 7:00 GMT hour. Too bad as I'd be up 174 pips. Need to learn patience. An EA or alert that would wake us up when it turns would be huge for this.  
  
2\. Since I'm just testing, I decided to watch all the JPY crosses. NZDJPY is developing a signal in the current hour (13:00 GMT) but I got so excited about the change that I went in early, not remembering to wait until the bar closes / open of the next one. Jury is still out on that one but is -19 right now.

  * [#181](/thread/post/1739552#post1739552 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 1, 2007 1:03am  Dec 1, 2007 1:03am 

  * [ Eureka](eureka)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [383 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=16246)

In the Navigator on the left hand side of the charts, find the 'Custom Indicators' section. Click on the little + before it, find the indicator by name, double click on it. Another box will appear, click on OK and it should appear on your below your chart.  
  
I hope this helps. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

  * [#190](/thread/post/1740180#post1740180 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 7:23pm  Dec 1, 2007 7:01pm | Edited 7:23pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar33035_4.gif) Scrat](scrat)

  * Joined Feb 2007 | Status: Trader | [3,719 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=33035)

there is something missing from this system.  
i have been using macd for quite some time now and i have to tell you this about macd histogram (or osma, it is the same thing): no matter what settings you use, there will always be times when you see divergences (either classical or hidden). so let's talk about this.  
a hidden divergence is the best opportunity to open a new position in the same direction as the main trend, so i'm not talking about this particular case. you make profit using the original rules.  
a very different situation happens when you see a classical divergence: you can't just trade it the way tk proposed in the original rules, because in this case price will always goes into the other direction. i mean, sure you can trade it, but wouldn't you better keep that 50 pips SL in your pocket?  
here's an example about what i am trying to say. g-j, h4. i am only talking about entry points, the value of SL/TP/TS is a different story...  
look at the blue vertical lines: you are buying on tops and selling on bottoms if you are using the original rules. all are fake signals.  
now look at the trendline: price is below it; then look at CCI, it is mostly below 0 (these are actually the 2 filters i wanted to suggest - trendlines and CCI).   
think about it.  
  
p.s. the vertical red line is an entry that would have brought just a few pips, probably less than 50 (after you move SL to b/e with 150 pips rule). you have 5 fake entries, and only one winner.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar4502_4.gif) james275](james275)

  * | Joined Nov 2005  | Status: Trader | [129 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=4502)

> [Quoting Scrat](/thread/post/1740185#post1740185 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> and another example, about a possible move on g-j.  
>  there is a beautiful setup on this h4 chart. bearish hidden divergence on osma...   
>  as soon as price breaks that trendline, take the short signal given by osma. it should bring you a very nice profit.

> Ignored

Scrat, nice seeing u again.   
  
U are so right about the divergence issue. We traders are a funny bunch as we try and refine things to make it work. I am doing the same as you. Trendline filter, MA filter, etc. The problem as i see it is that we (me) fail to see the big picture, and afraid to take a loss.   
  
Looking at the 4 hr GBY (that is what i trade personally as well) U show the 4 losers which is true but just before those is an 800 pip and 400 pip winner. And the current trade will be a winner too. From my calculations the winners significantly offset the losers. I need to finish my REAL backtest so i have a much better understanding of proformance. As much as i can tell, this is a very profitable system. So i am very hesitant to start changing a profitable system to just optimize it.   
  
BUT...can it be tweeked to rid us of some of those pesky false signals (see i am aready complicating it..!) ???  
  
Here is my thoughts on filters: I just have a hard time being a mechanical trader.   
  
1\. On a signal, take the breakout of that bar instead of close of it. i find that even a nice trend will have a rogue bar in the opposite direction, and this tends to help you stay in the trade and not take the false signal, just to have to take another signal on the next bar. Saves 2 [spreads](/brokers/spreads "View Live Spreads on the Broker Guide"). Real signals (like the last one on the 4 hr) are only impacted a bit.  
  
2\. Should we always be in market? I won't be in the market against a trend that i believe is continuing. So in those cases i don't take any signals in that direction. If i am in, i might get out, but i won't go in the opposite direction. That is discretionary on my part. If we are range bound, then i will go both ways. I will also look at price patterns. The chart you had showed a very nice higher low indicating a long may be appropriate.   
  
What i appreciate about this system is that it is simple and works. In fact, i am coming to believe that simplicity is a major factor in a traders success. So i am keeping that and only want to add a few discretionary items to tweek it more to my advantage. TK continually encourages us all to "make it your own".   
  
THanks for your observations.. ALso, for those trading the 4 hr/ daily/ weekly. I think 50 pip stop is too low. It works very well for the 1 hr time frame.   
  
Jimno 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#194](/thread/post/1740712#post1740712 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 2, 2007 11:57pm  Dec 2, 2007 11:57pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar33035_4.gif) Scrat](scrat)

  * Joined Feb 2007 | Status: Trader | [3,719 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=33035)

when i first read about a system, i don't look where it works but where it doesn't.   
this one is another trend following system and it will bring nice profits (as always) as long as we see a trend; so i don't bother with the profitable trades. what about when we don't have a trend, or when trend is changing? these are the conditions that will bring drawdowns, and before i use this system i would need to focus on these situations.   
most of you will probably say this: well, if the profits are big enough to compensate for the drawdowns, why bother? yes, true. but how do we know that we will have enough profits? we don't! and if you think about backtesting, it won't work; from my experience, backtesting is not relevant enough no matter how far you go in the past. it won't tell you about the future, because market conditions are constantly evolving. take this from a guy who spent weeks after weeks of backtesting.   
the only thing that works is MINIMIZE LOSSES, because you never know what your profits would be in the future. this is what this thread should be talking about. 

Nihil Sine Deo.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#195](/thread/post/1740734#post1740734 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 3, 2007 12:36am  Dec 3, 2007 12:36am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar33035_4.gif) Scrat](scrat)

  * Joined Feb 2007 | Status: Trader | [3,719 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=33035)

and now some comments on what you said.  
the breakout entry is a very good point. i always do this because i believe it is safer.  
no, we shouldn't always be in market. there are ranging & choppy conditions when it is better to stay out. i am a swing trader and i only feel comfortable "at large". now...   
that 50 pips SL doesn't work for g-j on h4 at all. i'm not even sure it works on h1 because most of the times i set stops of about 80-90 pips on this timeframe.  
there are many more things to discuss, but i don't think this is the place. this is not my strategy and if i come up with any change i consider important, it won't look at all like the original setup.   
  
p.s. by the way, i didn't find anything about this: after you are stopped, what is next? a new entry according to the rules? or just stand aside until...?

This may have been answered but I don't remember seeing it. When you are in a trade, but not stopped out, and the signal changes, what do you do.  
  
A. Exit the trade and open oen in the other direction  
B. Exit the trade and not re-enter  
C. Stay in the trade.  
  
I have been whipsawed today by CHFJPY when doing A. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#210](/thread/post/1743089#post1743089 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 5:53pm  Dec 4, 2007 5:19pm | Edited 5:53pm 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

You would exit and enter a new trade in the opposite direction. There are only two ways to exit a trade - either your stop loss/trailing stop is hit or you get a reverse signal.  
  
I agree that we need a filter for ranging markets. Some say that by taking every signal your profits from riding trends with the trailing stop will overshadow the numerous 50 pip losers....time will tell.  
  
Also in regards to re-entering a trade after being stopped out. My interpretation is that you would need to wait for the next _reverse_ signal. For example, if I was long and got stopped out, I would have to wait for the next short signal to appear. My reasoning for this is taken from Post #3 which states that you are "simply selling the peaks and buying at the trough" of the MACD or OsMA indicators. So if we went long at the trough of the OsMA/MACD indicator and got stopped out but the bars kept climbing higher then I could not enter long because we were no longer at the trough, we would now have to wait for a short signal at the next peak of the OsMA/MACD indicator.

First, my apologies to those who are losing it about people tweaking this fine system. I guess I thought that's what these forums were for.  
  
I've been trading this on the daily charts, and the way I've been avoiding whipsaws is to overlay 90-day linear regression lines on the chart. These lines will automatically and neatly show you the way the market is trending. I then only take trades in the direction of the trend.  
  
It's working so far.

I'm trying to avoid whipsaws by trading in only one direction, and the slope of the linear regression gives me an objective standard to decide which way to trade. I tried an 89 SMA first, but I think the regression lines are better.  
  
It's working so far. Not every trade gains, and some gains are bigger than others, but at least my transaction costs are reduced by not taking trades both ways. Does anyone smarter than me see anything conceptually wrong with this method?

  * [#240](/thread/post/1748577#post1748577 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 7, 2007 10:54am  Dec 7, 2007 10:54am 

  * [ TraderGeek](tradergeek)

  * | Joined Dec 2006  | Status: Trader | [220 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=29654)

I'm certainly no MQL guru but here is my attempt at adding Alerts and Email to the OsMA Color Indicator.   
  
Inputs Added:  
  
AlertOn: You want MT4 alerts  
EmailOn: You want MT4 to send email as configured in the platform  
  
Logic:  
All this does is compare the most recent closed bar (so 1 bar ago) to the one before that. If the color is different, it generates an alert/email that says the color changed. At that point it's up to you to do any other due diligence, wait for another bar to close, etc.  
  
Also, the alerting logic only runs once per bar, not per tick. So on the first tick of a newly opened bar, it looks at the prior two bars to detect a color change. It does not look at the newly opened bar at all. I thought of making sure it was the same color as the most recently closed bar, but decided not to as I think a lot of people are trading this system differently than others.  
  
I have done only the most rudimentary testing on this so YMMV. 

Attached File(s)

![File Type: mq4](https://assets.faireconomy.media/images/attach/mq4.gif) [OsMA Color2.mq4](/attachment/file/71238?d=1196996034) 5 KB | 853 downloads

However the year before that it actually lost -667 pips in all of 12 months before this 2007 profitable year. That's why a system might be great this year but how did it do previous years? A five year test is the minimum to test. Paris

i see no reason why it couldn't be used on any pair. if you pull the MACD/OSMA up on any pair, any timeframe it does the same thing.  
  
what you could do for example, is look at all the major pairs, on timeframes that suit you, and see which ones have nice clean trades (not too many swings)  
  
obviously this would be ongoing as the behaviour changes on the different pair/timeframe combinations.  
  
all the best!

you may be getting alerts every time the bar changes colour!  
  
as it crosses the previous bar price it will fluctuate while the price bounces around near that price, then once it moves far enough past in either direction it will stop.

I've been testing the system for two weeks now. Using a live account but with micro lots (.10 / pip). So consider it a live demo. Here are my results for the two weeks:  
  
Total Pips: 817  
  
Week 1: 434   
Week 2: 383   
  
**By pair**  
  
_Week 1_  
GBPUSD 279   
EURUSD 75   
USDCHF 75  
USDJPY 55  
GBPJPY -50  
  
_Week 2_  
GBPJPY 224  
GBPCHF 130  
USDJPY 109  
GBPUSD 19  
EURGBP 7  
EURUSD -40  
USDCHF -66  
  
Max Drawdown: 200 pips  
  
Two weeks is not much of a sample size but its enough for me to really like the system. I'm going to crank it up to 1 mini lot and run it for a few more weeks. Assuming all goes well I'll then put some real $ into it.  
  
Thanks TKimble for a great system.

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

Here's a copy of my trading plan from this system if anyone wants it. I've read the thread and believe I have incorporated all posts by TK.   
  
\------------------------------------------------------------------------  
  
_Trend Hugger_

  1. Trade on 1-hour, 4-hour, Daily, and Weekly charts 
  2. OSMA Color Indicator (Fast 40, Slow 50, Signal 100)

Trading Rules  
  
**Stop Loss = 50 pips**  
  
**Entry Rules**   
1. Enter long if:  
  
The prior OsMA trend was down and:  
  
a. The current OsMA bar is greater than the previous OsMA bar value.   
i. Enter on the close of the bar.  
  
Or  
  
b. The current OsMA bar is up and the previous two bars are of equal value you may enter before the close of the current bar.  
  
2. Enter short if:  
  
The prior OsMA trend was up and:  
  
a. The current OsMA bar is less than the previous OsMA bar value.   
i. Enter on the close of the bar.  
  
Or  
  
b. The current OsMA bar is down and the previous two bars are of equal value you may enter before the close of the current bar.  
  
**Exit Rules**  
  
_Â·_ When trade turns profitable by 150 pips then initiate a 150 pip trailing stop.  
_Â·_ Otherwise exit at the next signal (Stop and Reverse).

50 pip SL, but I will exit before that if the signal reverses. The drawdown is based on closed trades, so 4 losers in a row for example if they were all stopped out at 50 pips. I think it was more like 6 losers in a row but some were closed before the 50 pip mark.   
  
I didn't keep track of drawdown for open trades so I suppose it could have been more than the 200 at one point or another.

  * [#272](/thread/post/1762189#post1762189 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 10:57am  Dec 17, 2007 10:34am | Edited 10:57am 

  * [ smak74](smak74)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [4 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56439)

I paid an EA programmer to program this for us. What's a couple hundred dollars if you can make thousands right? Anyways I want to thank Tkimble for his system first of all and for sharing his knowledge with us. What a cool guy. Hopefully he sees this thread and will download the EA as a gift. I'll send him a message too. The orders will open up when the EA is initialized in the direction of the OSMA color. The EA will close the order once your stop loss is triggered, take profit triggered, or if the OSMA color changes and it will close the existing order and then open up a reverse order in the direction of the OSMA change. Its done pretty good for me so far but I am using a demo account. I like to activate it before the London opening and go to sleep because if you notice the past couple weeks that is the period some major moves are made. The EA has worked pretty good so far.   
  
I like to use the 30 min charts since the OSMA colors to change that much and am able to catch a move sooner than the 1 hour charts.   
  
Here are the pairs I run the EA on simultaneously there are probably more but these are the ones I use:  
  
AUD/USD  
GBP/CHF  
GBP/JPY  
GBP/USD  
EUR/USD  
USD/CHF  
  
I didn't program this so don't ask me to change it. Maybe a EA programmer like Skyline can adjust it if needed but it works pretty good. The only thing I'd like to hear from you guys is how its working for you.   
  
Thanks again Tkimble YOU ROCK!!

  * [#275](/thread/post/1762389#post1762389 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 17, 2007 2:08pm  Dec 17, 2007 2:08pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar46998_4.gif) crapola](crapola)

  * | Joined Aug 2007  | Status: Trader | [22 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=46998)

Overall, it works very well! I used 150 pip TS and 65 pip SL in my testing. One problem though that would prevent me from using it live:  
  
"The orders will open up when the EA is initialized in the direction of the OSMA color."   
  
This causes the EA to open a trade immediately upon initialization as it doesn't wait for a fresh signal. Also, if a trade hit the SL but the direction hasn't changed, it will open up another trade. This deviates from tkimble's method by buy at the highs and selling at the troughs. I did find it to cause some major drawdown at times due to multiple losses in a row. If the SL gets hit multiple times, and the direction hasn't changed, chances are the market is too volatile and it is best to stay out.   
  
If this is an intended feature, can you or someone with MQ4 programming experience add a "enter on fresh signal" option?  
  
Thanks again for posting this, that was very generous of you. 

crapola

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#276](/thread/post/1763171#post1763171 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 17, 2007 11:24pm  Dec 17, 2007 11:24pm 

  * [ smak74](smak74)

  * | Joined Dec 2007  | Status: Trader | [4 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=56439)

I see what you mean unfortunately I can't program it in. Maybe someone here can adjust. In choppy days on 30 min the color changes too much and since the EA closes out your existing orders and opens up a reverse order when the color changes. This loses us money. It is best to use the EA on a 1hr chart where the color doesn't change so frequently an when it does it is usually with the trend. This is Tkimbles preferred trade time anyways.

  * Edited 7:11am  Dec 18, 2007 6:57am | Edited 7:11am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar46998_4.gif) crapola](crapola)

> [Quoting smak74](/thread/post/1763171#post1763171 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I see what you mean unfortunately I can't program it in. Maybe someone here can adjust. In choppy days on 30 min the color changes too much and since the EA closes out your existing orders and opens up a reverse order when the color changes. This loses us money. It is best to use the EA on a 1hr chart where the color doesn't change so frequently an when it does it is usually with the trend. This is Tkimbles preferred trade time anyways.
> 
> Ignored

I'm really referring to when the color hasn't changed. If it stops out, and the color is still the same, it will open up an order at the next bar. In other words, there will always be a continuous trade opened up. Instead, if a trade gets stopped out, it should wait for the next color change and open it in that direction. This is mostly observed when initially attaching the EA to the chart as it will immediately open a trade at the next bar -- it should wait for a fresh signal (reversal in the color). 

crapola

if you double click or right click on it on NAVIGATOR->EA-> MODIFY on it it opens metaeditor and beginning looks like this, which is self-explanatory. i don't know about programming.   
  
  
you can back-test it.   
unfortunately results are alwasy negative (as CRAPOLA said), profit factor is btw 0.5-0.8 (it means you LOSE MONEY), for reasons discussed at at pages 18-19 of the thread.  
sorry SMAK74, method is good, but indicator doesn't work like it is supposed to do, because of color change in the middle of the OsMA bars.  
please don't use it live in current form otherwise you will lose all of your account. Try demo for 1 month, you have nothing to lose this way.   
  
  
#property link "http://www.mqlservice.com"  
  
//+---- Programmed by Michal Rutka @ MQLService.com  
  
\-----------------+  
//--- OSMA parameters  
extern int FastEMA=40;  
extern int SlowEMA=50;  
extern int SignalSMA=100;  
extern int FridayCloseHour=20;  
//--- Standard parameters  
extern double Lots = 0.1;  
extern double TradeMaxRisk = 0; // TradeMaxRisk > 0 so much % risk will be used, either based on SL or Account equity  
extern int StopLoss = 50; // 0 deactivates Stop Loss  
extern int StartTrail = 0; // Start trail after so many pips.  
extern int TrailingStop = 0; // 0 deactivates Trailing Stop  
extern int TakeProfit = 0; // 0 deactivates Take Profit  
extern int GainForBE = 0; // How many pips will trigger Break Even. 0 deactivates.  
extern int PipsBE = 0; // Level at which Break Even will be put  
extern int StartTime = 700; // Start trading at 7:00  
extern int StopTime = 700; // Stop trading at 23:00; Set to StartTime for continous operation (default).  
extern int Slippage = 3; 

Once A Trader Always A Trader.

Here's an EA I developed using Expert Advisor Builder.   
  
Its been set to look for a peak and valley, then buy and sell accordingly.   
  
Peak: The past three bars are as follows: 1<2>3  
Valley: The past three bars are as follows: 1>2<3

Well, here's what I'm doing with it.   
  
I just put it on any chart under 1 hr. (30 min, 15 min, etc.), but get the OSMA/MACD reading from the 1 hr chart. That way, it checks for a reversal at specific intervals, (1 min, 5 min, etc.) Hopefully that can reduce whipsawing.   
  
If you would like to make your own variations, google "Expert Advisor Builder" It's a fairly simple interface, and is perfect for those small and relatively simple trading systems: something tkimble is famous for. That's what I use to make the foundation of my EAs, I use my own coding skills to tweak it.   
  
Tkimble mentioned something about MACD/OSMA being equal and therefore triggering a signal. If that really is a stronger signal, then can someone please elaborate on how it works? Where is the equal portion on the 3 bar reversal signal? On the current bar? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#297](/thread/post/1770434#post1770434 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 22, 2007 5:48am  Dec 22, 2007 5:48am 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

Heres my understanding of the "equal bars" rule:  
  
I'll use an example for going long:  
  
If the OSMA trend is down;  
followed by two bars of equal value;  
and now the current bar is up (meaning that it is higher than the two equal bars);  
then you can enter long BEFORE THE CLOSE of the current bar.  
  
The reason for this, according to TK, is that once the current bar CLOSES HIGHER it usually causes the second bar, of the two equal bars, to CHANGE ITS VALUE HIGHER. I believe this concept is called "repainting".  
  
You're essentially anticipating that the previous bar will repaint itself higher, thus giving you a proper entry signal. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#298](/thread/post/1770668#post1770668 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 22, 2007 11:05am  Dec 22, 2007 11:05am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Based on your explanation, I'm basically looking for the same setup as in my other EAs, but instead of looking at the shape at the close of the bar, I look at the current value.  
  
For example, a "BUY" signal means that the past 3 bars are (1 is current)   
1>2<3 for BOTH the MACD and OSMA, and both the MACD and OSMA are equal.   
  
For a "SELL" signal, the past three bars are 1<2>3 , and both MACD and OSMA are equal.   
  
  
Did I get that right? If so, I'll set up an EA which will look only for those signals. If they really are more powerful, it may improve the system. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#299](/thread/post/1770942#post1770942 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 23, 2007 3:22am  Dec 23, 2007 3:22am 

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

If I were to write the "equal bar" rule into a program (and I'm no programer!) I would format it into something like this:  
  
Note: I would use 4 bars. Bar 1 is the current bar. Bars 2 and 3 are the "equal bars". Bar 4 is the bar before bar 3 which we will use to determine the trend _prior to the "equal bars" formation_. Also, when I talk about bars, I'm talking about the OsMA/MACD bars - not price bars.  
  
Enter long if:  
  
4 > 3 _and_ 3 = 2 _and_ 2 < 1  
  
You're basically looking for a "U" shaped formation where Bar 4 is the left side, Bars 3 and 2 are the middle arch, and Bar 1 is the right side.  
  
I also must stress that this is _my interpretation_ of the "equal bars" rule from TK's Post #112 and confirmed in Posts #118 and #119. Also I don't recall TK saying that this signal was more powerful then a simple reversal - I believe he said that it just allows you to get a jump on an anticipated reversal signal. Obviously this has the advantage of getting in with a better price/stop though. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#300](/thread/post/1771135#post1771135 "Post Permalink")

  * Dec 23, 2007 12:49pm  Dec 23, 2007 12:49pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

Lincoln,   
  
Based on your response, I'll assume that this other signal explained by TKimble looks for a 4 bar "U" as opposed to a 3 bar "V"  
  
  
So, a buy signal is (1 is current bar):  
  
1>2  
2=3  
3<4  
  
  
A sell signal is:  
  
1<2  
2=3  
3>4  
  
  
  
Here is an explanation of the variable:   
  
OSMA_PeriodMinutes = 60; The time in minutes that you want the OSMA to be based on.   
  
  
The rest should be self-explanatory.   
  
  
  
Let's assume that I wanted this EA to use the 1 hr chart, and look for the "U" formation every 15 mins.   
  
I would open up a 15min chart, attach this EA, and make sure that the OSMA_PeriodMinutes is set to 60 (60 minutes = 1 hour).  
  
Lincoln, is that what you're looking for?

1<2  
2<=3  
3>4  
  
In any case, I ran a back test and no trades opened on the 15 min chart. The original EA made plenty of trades, even though it wasn't based completely on tkimble's logic.  
  
Mark

Notice the attached chart has the period grayed out. This will allow us to ignore false entries. CCI will keep diversion in check too. Execute a buy when CCI is above or cross above zero and a sell when CCI is below or crosses below zero.

1>2  
2<=3  
3<4  
  
SELL:  
  
1<2  
2>=3  
3>4  
  
  
Your method looked primarily for a "U" signal, this modified version looks primarily for a "V" signal.

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

I don't know how the backtests are conducted but I should note that if the backtest relies on looking at historical charts then you wont get many signals. The reason for this is because of the repainting that takes place after an "equal bar" signal is given.  
  
For example lets say Bar 4's value equals .00028, Bar's 3 and 2 equal .00025, and bar 1 currently equals .00027. This is a valid signal. However now lets say bar 1 _closes_ at .00027. If we were to look back at bar 2 it may not have the same value of .00025 that it originally had, it may be .00026 because of the _repainting_. Basically the higher closing value of bar 1 has changed the value of bar 2 even though it had already closed.   
  
Therefore if you were to look back at a historical chart for this particular trade bar 4 would equal .00028, bar 3 would equal .00025, bar 2 would equal .00026, and bar 1 would equal .00027. You would never know that bars 3 and 2 had once been equal!  
  
This is the essence of the "equal bars" rule, because bar 2 can change its value after the fact, and thus making it the actual reversal bar. If we were to wait for the close of bar 1 we would actually be entering _two bars late_ once bar 2 repaints itself higher! 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

The readout on the MACD is exactly the same shape as the OSMA. The main difference is the position relative to 0.   
  
All we're looking for on each indicator is when the slope changes from positive to negative.

I really hope this thread doesn't die. I want to continue learning from others on this system and how they are doing. I started trading live last week and have followed a method that filters divergence which appears to be the main issue here. Otherwise, this system appears to be extremely profitable. I think the discussions around EA's are fine and I like them as well but I don't want to lose the main focus here which is the methodology that TK outlined for us.   
  
I'm using the OsMA as designed but when we get a period of low volatility there are numerous false signals. Looking out for narrow bollinger bands seem to keep divergence in check and the CCI helps with good entries. If you look at a previous chart I posted, the gray areas in the bollinger squeeze indicator correspond with the narrow bands. However, you can miss a good break out while bands are still narrow. At this point, I will look at CCI (set to 24) and watch for it to near the 200 mark. Even during narrow bands, this yields very little false signals. Had I traded strictly by the OsMA, I would have had 6+ false entries in a row, but with the bollinger squeeze indicator, it would have only been 2. 

crapola

  * [ Lincoln10](lincoln10)

  * | Joined Nov 2007  | Status: Trader | [54 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=54725)

One way of determining the bollinger squeeze is to look for when Bollinger Bands (20,2) trade inside Keltner Channels (20,1.5). You would not trade while they are in this area as it means there is very low volatility.   
  
There's more to the squeeze play than this but since we're only looking to avoid periods of low volatility, the above info is all we need.  
  
Heres a simplified equation to use to know when to avoid trades:  
  
Upper Bollinger Band Channel < Upper Keltner Channel   
Lower Bollinger Band Channel > Lower Keltner Channel 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

The rules I am using are listed below. I have backtested this method with good success for the past few months. Also, a 50 pip SL appears to stop out too many good trades on my 6 pip spread IBFX account, so I have increased it to 65. I can post some additional charts for entries (exits are the same as tkimble's) if it seems helpful.  
  
enter long trades  
1) if OsMA is new color in up direction at closed bar and when Bollinger Squeeze w/ CCI is not gray and is above zero or crossing above zero  
entry exception: if Bollinger Squeeze w/ CCI is gray but is near 200 line.  
  
exit long trades  
1) if OsMA has changed color on closed bar or reached 65 pip SL  
  
enter short trades  
1) if OsMA is new color in down direction at closed bar and Bollinger Squeeze w/ CCI is not gray and is below zero or crossing below zero  
entry exception: if Bollinger Squeeze w/ CCI is gray but is near 200 line.  
  
exit short trades  
1) if OsMA has changed color on closed bar or reached 65 pip SL 

crapola

>  From what I can tell, it entered properly, it didn't stop and reverse like it should have.   
>    
>  Which EA are you using?  
>  Also, are you using my version of Bollinger squeeze? I had to modify the original indicator in order for it to interface better with the EA.
> 
> Ignored

  
I was using the crapola version. Also, I didn't realize that the indicator was different. I'll try that one and let you know how it goes. Thanks again for spending the time putting this together. 

crapola

  * [#327](/thread/post/1781496#post1781496 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 3, 2008 6:31am  Jan 3, 2008 6:31am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43541_7.gif) Ronald Raygun](ronald*raygun)

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

MMk, here's a rundown of the EAs.  
  
Version 1:This version uses only the "V" formation  
  
(Post 291)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=291](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1767622&postcount=291)  
(Post 293)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=293](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1769157&postcount=293)  
  
Version 2:This version looks for the Equal bar system. Either primarily a V formation, or primarily a U formation. (Based on the title).   
  
(Post 311)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=311](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1772282&postcount=311)  
  
Version 3: This version uses the bollinger squeeze method to filter out any sideways movement.   
  
(Post 319)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=319](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1777444&postcount=319)  
  
OSMA-BasedCrapolaU_Primary uses the U Primary method with the bolinger squeeze.  
  
OSMA-BasedCrapolaV_Primary uses the V Primary method with the bollinger squeeze.   
  
Bollinger Squeeze v7 is my version which is required for any of these EAs to work. Make sure that this is in the indicator folder.   
  
OSMA-BasedCrapola is the V only method like version 1.  
  
  
  
  
That should be a complete listing of all the versions I made.  
  
  
  
I use the OSMA-Based EA as it works best for me. Quite minimal and easy to hunt for bugs when debugging. Just now I closed on a 250 pip gain, so. If it ain't broke, don't fix it.

Yep! MACD and OSMA are exactly the same thing. The only real difference is the position relative to 0  
  
Since this trading system is looking for a particular shape, it doesn't matter which you use. Although I prefer OSMA primarily because it's easier to program with.

I am trading with an $1000 account using the original EA I programmed.   
  
My results are pretty modest myself. The Ea was active since 12/25/2007 and has since gone from $1000 to 1220.36. A very modest return, but certainly much better than other things I'm doing.   
  
The profit factor thus far is 2.4 That means that for every dollar I lose, I make $2.40.   
  
This is running on a 1 HR tf of GBPJPY and it's working fine for me. It seems to miss a few signals, but I'm guessing that's a result of repainting.

  * [#343](/thread/post/1786868#post1786868 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 7, 2008 1:04am  Jan 7, 2008 1:04am 

  * [ currymonster](currymonster)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: Trader | [92 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=34011)

> [Quoting ducks](/thread/post/1786745#post1786745 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I am sorry to ask you this but hope do you do this?  
>  but how do you put them on the mt4 flatform  
>  I am new to this stuff  
>    
>  thank-you
> 
> Ignored

Try this :-  
  
Copy and Paste the indicators into the "experts/indicators" folder where you installed MT4.  
For example, if you downloaded the installer from Strategybuilderfx.com, you'll paste the indicators in the ff. folder:  
C:\Program Files\StrategyBuilderFX 4\experts\indicators  
Or if you downloaded it from metaquotes.net, you'll paste it here:  
C:\Program Files\MetaTrader 4\experts\indicators  
  
  
If MT4 is currently open, close it.  
  
Now, Re-Open MT4  
  
In the navigator window under experts click on the custom indicator Tab and choose the indicator you want from the list.  
  
Hope this helps,  
  
by the way there's a very helpful search facility at the top of the forex factory page which helps when you need to find things.  
  
Happy pipping,  
  
cal

  * Jan 17, 2008 2:51pm  Jan 17, 2008 2:51pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar37993_2.gif) SteveHopwood](stevehopwood)

  * | Commercial User  | Joined Apr 2007 | [8,331 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=37993)

Somebody asserted in an earlier thread that this strategy would be badly hit by whipsaw. I found out just how badly when I started to demo-trade last week.  
  
Thursday was great - made a shed-load of pips.  
  
Friday - whipsaw took them all back and some more.  
  
Monday and Tuesday - more modest loss.  
  
Come yesterday, Wednesday, I decided to try adding one of the filters posted here, so I added the Bollinger Squeaze.  
  
By following the simple rule of only entering a trade on an OsMA bar colour change that was matched by the same colour in the corresponding Bollinger bar I avoided most of the bad trades - 1h tf and checking on progress every hour.  
  
The effect was dramatic. For a couple of hours in the afternoon, I had 5 trades open, all heading in the right direction. At one point, I could have closed out having tripled the account balance - had this been live I would have done this, for sure.  
  
Being a demo, I set a 50 pip trailing stop and sat back to watch. Gradually, the orders peaked and retraced to the sl. Four of the orders closed leaving the account balance double what it had been at the start of the day  
.  
There was one trade left open - a uc buy. This is still open as I write this on Thursday morning, and cannot make less than +59 whatever happens now. It was fascinating to watch uc scream upwards yesterday; in the space of about an hour it shot up over 100 pips, slicing through resistance lines as though they had no psychological effect on traders whatever.  
  
uc hit its highest of 1.1023 and has stayed between this and about 1.1979 since, so it will be interesting to see which way it will go when it finally breaks the shackles. Given that uc is at, or very close to, its lowest ever (a glance at a monthly chart shows this) I am hoping it will breakout upwards. We shall see.  
  
It is early days. Who knows? Perhaps this week I will be writing, "Forget filtering the trades, it is a rubbish idea"? For now, applying a filter seems to help avoid whipsaw.  
  
![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f601.png?v=15.1)

  * [#362](/thread/post/1812855#post1812855 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 22, 2008 2:07am  Jan 22, 2008 2:07am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43318_4.gif) Pidgeon](pidgeon)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Seasoned Lurker | [242 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43318)

Two things....if you are trading this on a larger timeframe, say daily, then 100-200 pips isnt massive. Its normal for a day's work for many pairs.  
  
Secondly, If you want this to be a trend following system, then you wouldn't really want to set a TP at all. You get out when either the trend reverses itself (using OsMA or another indicator) or when it hits your trailing SL.  
  
A TP goes against the rule of letting profitable trades run....yes? 

Disregard all prognostications.

  * [#366](/thread/post/1827981#post1827981 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 31, 2008 4:28am  Jan 31, 2008 4:28am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43318_4.gif) Pidgeon](pidgeon)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Seasoned Lurker | [242 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43318)

I opened 3 trades using this system last friday (25th). Even with all the Fed hoopla, I'm up over 100 pips each on two of the pairs. The third, GBP/CHF, has been ranging but is looking to move up soon.   
  
I am very interested this week to see how trades opened here fare during major news events, so this is a good week to test this. My hope is that news is largely ignored against the momentum of the trend. I trade this on daily charts, so any news event tends to get absorbed anyway.  
  
So far, as TK has said, this is my most profitable system to date. Ok, well its not MY system but you get the drift. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1) TK's previous weekly scalping system was good, except that it suffered during ranging weeks. This system usually has you either in an existing trade or sitting out the pair while markets are ranging, so the range behavior should occur above or below your initial entry, allowing you to ride it out until the trend resumes.   
  
You do have to watch swap rates with the daily charts, and I've noticed some bias towards pairs with positive swap. 

Disregard all prognostications.
