  * [ sola_eleko](sola_eleko)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: Trader | [5 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=34097)

Ronald, Thanks for all your contributions. Which of the EAs is oSMA based, is it 291, 293 or 311. i want to know since this is the one you are using. thanks  
Sola  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
  
MMk, here's a rundown of the EAs.  
  
Version 1:This version uses only the "V" formation  
  
(Post 291)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=291](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1767622&postcount=291)  
(Post 293)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=293](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1769157&postcount=293)  
  
Version 2:This version looks for the Equal bar system. Either primarily a V formation, or primarily a U formation. (Based on the title).   
  
(Post 311)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=311](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1772282&postcount=311)  
  
Version 3: This version uses the bollinger squeeze method to filter out any sideways movement.   
  
(Post 319)  
[http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost...&postcount=319](http://www.forexfactory.com/showpost.php?p=1777444&postcount=319)  
  
OSMA-BasedCrapolaU_Primary uses the U Primary method with the bolinger squeeze.  
  
OSMA-BasedCrapolaV_Primary uses the V Primary method with the bollinger squeeze.   
  
Bollinger Squeeze v7 is my version which is required for any of these EAs to work. Make sure that this is in the indicator folder.   
  
OSMA-BasedCrapola is the V only method like version 1.  
  
  
  
  
That should be a complete listing of all the versions I made.  
  
  
  
I use the OSMA-Based EA as it works best for me. Quite minimal and easy to hunt for bugs when debugging. Just now I closed on a 250 pip gain, so. If it ain't broke, don't fix it.  

[](http://www.forexfactory.com/newreply.php?do=newreply&p=1781496)<http://www.forexfactory.com/images/buttons/quote.gif>

All of the EAs are OSMA-based, and the ones my server is running is on post 293.

  * Feb 12, 2008 12:35am  Feb 12, 2008 12:35am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43318_4.gif) Pidgeon](pidgeon)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Seasoned Lurker | [242 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43318)

> [Quoting bob_inabottle](/thread/post/1837285#post1837285 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi Pidgeon, How did those trades work out? im thinking the longer time frames are better. At the mo im using the 4hr..... had a bit of a go on the daily, still really not sure.  
>    
>  Thanks   
>    
>  Bob
> 
> Ignored

  
Hi Bob -   
  
I use the daily charts because trends seem easier to follow, and most pro traders use the daily charts. However there are not as many trades for this system as lower timeframes. TK uses hourly charts for this system, as he wants to stay busy and apparently doesn't have a regular job ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f633.png?v=15.1) like the rest of us.  
  
I am using 2xATR as a stop loss on all trades. Since we have been in a ranging pattern the last week or so on many pairs, I've been stopped out on 1 of the trades (Cable), and its come within a few pips of my stop twice on GBP/CHF. On my AUD/JPY trade, I closed it within a couple days of opening it, because I realized the volume was very low on this pair, and I felt a little overexposed on a pair i wasn't familiar with.  
  
I believe I will tighten my stops, so as to be stopped out sooner during ranging weeks. Better to stay out than to stay in a trade going nowhere. The GBP/CHF trade is still on from Jan 25th, but the price really never moved either way from the 30th to now.   
  
TK also uses his weekly scalp system, and it works well when the market is ranging as long is there is directional movement from M-F. This is a good system to work with while waiting for trends to resume. I believe trend following is still the best way to catch major market movements, but at the current time, most pairs are consolidating. Take a look at the daily chart of EUR/USD, we are stuck at 1.47, bouncing up and down and returning to it. Yen is stuck at 106.70 for the last two weeks. Etc. 

Disregard all prognostications.

  * Joined Jul 2007 | Status: 33 y/o Investor/Trader/Programmer | [5,016 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43541)

The system makes money, no doubt, but as with the vast majority of systems for free on FF, you need to understand where the system thrives, and to make sure that the system is in it's element. All of tKimble's systems require a highly defind trend to make money. So, avoid any pairs or other situations where it's ranging.  
  
  
This one is similar to the OzFx system, but aims for longer (3-week) trends.

not sure if you're still looking, but i'm looking to use it. I added in a 200SMA on the 1D so if it its above the 200SMA on Day I looking for buys on 1h and below 200SMA on day i look for sells only. Then I look at VWAP for entery, wait for it to be above the 50 period vwap on sell and below on but and then look at no lag MACD indicator to enter... seems pretty solid so far. looking at 20 to 30 PIP stop and 3:1 or 5:1 reward to risk. still looking. would love to look at this more with others if anyone is interested.
